```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)

4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

{"content":"1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference pa
... (truncated)

## Summary of Generated Documentation

### **Key Sections:**

1. **Overview** - Context about the v1.30→v1.31 changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Route cache control behavior refinement
3. **Deprecated Features** - `disable_clear_route_cache` field deprecation
4. **New Features** - Four major additions:
   - `RouteCacheAction` enum (DEFAULT, CLEAR, RETAIN)
   - Observability mode ("Send and Go" for non-blocking processing)
   - `deferred_close_timeout` for stream lifecycle management
   - `filter_metadata` for logging/observability
5. **Configuration Updates** - Step-by-step migration with examples
6. **Migration Steps** - Practical 6-step deployment process
7. **Testing Recommendations** - Unit and integration test scenarios
8. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur
9. **Behavioral Changes Summary** - Tables showing differences
10. **Reference Documentation** - Code locations and file references
11. **FAQ** - Common questions answered

### **Specific Changes Identified:**

| Change | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 |
|--------|---------|---------|
| Route Cache Control | `disable_clear_route_cache` (bool) | `route_cache_action` (enum: DEFAULT/CLEAR/RETAIN) |
| Observability Mode | ❌ Not available | ✅ New `observability_mode` field |
| Stream Closure | Immediate | Deferred (configurable, default 5s) |
| Filter Metadata | ❌ Not available | ✅ New `filter_metadata` field |

The guide includes:
- **Before/after configuration examples** for each feature
- **Code references** pointing to exact file locations and line numbers
- **Validation logic** preventing both old and new fields from being set simul

// * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. Envoy will send the\n91: // server\n92: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n93: // messages, and the server must reply with\n94: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n95: //\n96: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n97: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n98: // name.\n99: //\n100: // [#next-free-field: 18]\n101: message ExternalProcessor {\n102:   reserved 4;\n103: \n104:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n105: \n106:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n107:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n108:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n109: \n110:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n111:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n112:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n113:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n114:   // downstream client will be reset.\n115:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n116:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n117:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n118: \n119:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n120:   // sent. There will be no\n200:   // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n201:   bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n202: \n203:   // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n204:   MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n205: \n206:   // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n207:   // without pausing on filter chain iteration. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n254:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n255: }\n256: \n257: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n258: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n259: //\n260: // This works as below:\n261: //\n262: //   1. (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\\n229:   // This also means that\\n230:   // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\\n231:   // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\\n232:   //\\n233:   // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\\n234:   //\\n235:   // .. warning::\\n236:   //\\n237:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\\n238:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\\n239:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\\n240:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\\n241:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\\n242:   //\\n243:   bool observability_mode = 17;\\n244: \\n245:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\\n246:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n247:   // field is set in an external processor response.\\n248:   // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\\n249:   // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\\n250:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\\n251:       [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \\\"clear_route_cache_type\\\"];\\n252: \\n253:   // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\\n254:   // received in response to request headers. It is recommended to set this field than set\\n255:   // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`.\\n256:   // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\\n257:   RouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\\n258:       [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \\\"clear_route_cache_type\\\"];\\n259: \\n260:   // Specifies the deferred closure timeout for gRPC stream that connects to external processor. Currently, the deferred stream closure\\n261:   // is only used in :ref:`observability_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`.\\n262:   // In observability mode, gRPC streams may be held open to the external processor longer than the lifetime of the regular client to\\n263:   // backend stream lifetime. In this case, Envoy will eventually timeout the external processor stream according to this time limit.\\n264:   // The default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified.\\n265:   google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\\n266: }\\n267: \\n268: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\\n269: // dynamic metadata. This allows\\n279:     // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\\n280:     // definition for safe parsing.\\n281:     repeated string typed = 2;\\n282:   }\\n283: \\n284:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\\n285:   // the external processing server.\\n286:   MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\\n287: \\n288:   // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\\n289:   // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\\n290:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\\n291:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\\n292: }\\n293: \\n294: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\\n295: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n296: //\\n297: // This works as below:\\n298: //\\n299: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\\n300: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\\n301: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n302: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\\n303: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n304: //   4.     "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n8: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n9: import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n10: \n11: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n12: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";\n15: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n16: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n17: \n18: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n19: option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\n21: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. The metadata\n200:   // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n201:   // ext_proc filter name.\n202:   google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n203: \n204:   // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n205:   // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n206:   // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n207:   // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n208:   // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n209:   bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n210: \n211:   // If set to true, ignore the\n212:   // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n213:   // message in an external processor response. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\\n30: \\n31: Statistics\\n32: ----------\\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\\n35: <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\\n36: comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\\n37: \\n38: The following statistics are supported:\\n39: \\n40: .. csv-table::\\n41:   :header: Name, Type, Description\\n42:   :widths: auto\\n43: \\n44:   streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\\n45:   streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\\n46:   streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\\n47:   spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\\n48:   streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\\n49:   streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\\n50:   failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\\n51:   message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\\n52:   rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\\n53:   clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\\n54:   clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\\n55: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--50ea83e6@1ee8aa56b83277e4f804bb70a12461d54ad68fa5/-/blob/docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst\"}",

    "content": "1: .. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n2: \n3: External Processing\n4: ===================\n5: * This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n6: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n7: \n8: The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n9: to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\\n30: \\n31: Statistics\\n32: ----------\\n33: This filter outputs statistics in the\\n34: ``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace.   "content": "# Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) Filter Migration Guide\n## Version 1.30.0 to 1.31.0\n\n---\n\n## 1. Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 (April 2024)** to **version 1.31.0 (July 2024)**.\n\nThe ext_proc filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses through a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy v1.31.0 introduces several enhancements focused on:\n\n- **Fine-grained route cache control** via a new `RouteCacheAction` enum\n- **Observability/monitoring mode** (\"Send and Go\") for non-blocking external processing\n- **Deferred stream closure** with configurable timeouts for clean resource management\n- **Better configuration semantics** with deprecation of boolean flags in favor of explicit enum values\n\n### Scope of Changes\n\nAll changes are in the **filter configuration API** and **internal stream management**. The external processor's gRPC service interface (ProcessingRequest/ProcessingResponse) remains unchanged.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 Route Cache Management Behavior Change\n\n**Change Type:** Configuration Option Deprecation + Behavior Refinement\n\n**Proto Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\nIn v1.30.0, route cache clearing was controlled by a single boolean field:\n\n```proto\n// v1.30.0\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n```\n\nIn v1.31.0, this has been superseded by an explicit enum with three options:\n\n```proto\n// v1.31.0\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Default: Obey the clear_route_cache flag from the external processor response\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear route cache (ignore clear_route_cache response flag)\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear route cache (ignore clear_route_cache response flag)\n  // Equivalent to old: disable_clear_route_cache = true\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n```\n\n**Impact:**\n- The old `disable_clear_route_cache` field is still accepted but **deprecated**\n- v1.31.0 automatically converts `disable_clear_route_cache=true` to `route_cache_action=RETAIN`\n- Using both fields with non-default values simultaneously is **not allowed** and will cause a validation error\n\n**Migration Example:**\n\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 - Disable route cache clearing\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# v1.31.0 - Equivalent configuration (recommended)\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Validation Details:**\n- If `disable_clear_route_cache=true` is specified, it's converted to `route_cache_action=RETAIN` (lines 213-221, ext_proc.cc)\n- If both fields have non-DEFAULT/non-true values, the config will be **rejected** with error:\n  ```\n  \"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\"\n  ```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 disable_clear_route_cache Field\n\n**Status:** Deprecated (but still functional for backward compatibility)\n\n**Timeline:** This field is marked for removal in a future Envoy version (likely v1.32+)\n\n**Migration Path:**\n\n| Old Config (`v1.30.0`) | New Config (`v1.31.0`) | Behavior |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Follow clear_route_cache flag from processor |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Always ignore clear_route_cache flag |\n\n**Code References:**\n- v1.31.0 FilterConfig constructor: Lines 213-221 in `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n- Proto field with migrate annotation: Lines 250-251 in `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Deprecation Note:** The field is annotated with `field_migrate` annotation in the proto, indicating Envoy's intention to promote `route_cache_action` as the canonical field.\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 RouteCacheAction Enum\n\n**Added in:** v1.31.0\n\n**Purpose:** Provide explicit, semantic control over route cache clearing behavior in response to processor modifications.\n\n**Usage:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # or DEFAULT, RETAIN\n```\n\n**Three Options:**\n\n1. **DEFAULT (0)** - Follow the processor response\n   - If processor sets `clear_route_cache=true` in response headers \u2192 clear cache\n   - Otherwise \u2192 keep cache as-is\n   - This is the default behavior if not specified\n\n2. **CLEAR (1)** - Always clear the route cache\n   - Route cache is cleared whenever the processor returns with header mutations\n   - Used when the processor frequently modifies headers that affect routing decisions\n   - Ensures routes are recomputed immediately\n\n3. **RETAIN (2)** - Never clear the route cache\n   - Route cache clearing requests from the processor are ignored\n   - Processor's `clear_route_cache` flag in CommonResponse is disregarded\n   - Useful when external processing doesn't affect routing\n\n**Implementation Details:**\n- Logic in `DecodingProcessorState::handleCommonHeaderResponse()` (processor_state.cc, lines 440-461)\n- The behavior only applies to downstream traffic (not upstream)\n- Route cache is only cleared when header mutations are present in the response\n\n---\n\n### 4.2 Observability Mode (\"Send and Go\")\n\n**Added in:** v1.31.0\n\n**Purpose:** Allow external processors to observe traffic without blocking the main request processing flow.\n\n**Configuration:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5000ms  # optional, default: 5000ms\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n\n| Aspect | Details |\n|--------|---------|\n| **Request Handling** | Messages sent to processor without waiting for responses |\n| **Response Blocking** | No blocking; filter continues processing immediately |\n| **Body Modes** | Only STREAMED mode is supported; BUFFERED/BUFFERED_PARTIAL ignored |\n| **Stream Closure** | Streams are deferred-closed after `deferred_close_timeout` |\n| **Use Case** | Logging, monitoring, security observability without latency impact |\n\n**Important Warnings:**\n- Flow control is **not yet implemented**\n- Fast senders (clients/servers) can overwhelm slow processors\n- Manual flow control implementation recommended in the processor service\n- See GitHub issue #33319 for flow control development status\n\n**Example Use Case:**\n```yaml\n# Monitor all traffic without affecting latency\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: security_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n**Implementation:**\n- Managed by `ThreadLocalStreamManager` and `DeferredDeletableStream` (ext_proc.h, lines 148-199)\n- Deferred closure uses Envoy dispatcher timers (ext_proc.cc, line 1384)\n- Observability mode logic in `Filter::sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` (ext_proc.cc, line 644+)\n\n---\n\n### 4.3 Deferred Close Timeout\n\n**Added in:** v1.31.0\n\n**Purpose:** Control how long gRPC streams to external processors remain open after the request/response completes.\n\n**Configuration:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5000ms  # 5 seconds (default)\n```\n\n**Details:**\n- **Default Value:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n- **Valid Range:** 0 to 3600000 milliseconds (0 to 1 hour)\n- **Used In:** Observability mode and other scenarios requiring extended stream lifetime\n- **Purpose:** Prevent abrupt stream closure and allow graceful cleanup of resources\n\n**When It Matters:**\n- In observability mode, streams may outlive the HTTP request/response cycle\n- Allows processors to complete logging/monitoring work before disconnection\n- Prevents server-side processing errors from abrupt closure\n\n**Proto Field:**\n```proto\ngoogle.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n```\n\n**Example:**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Allow 10 seconds for deferred stream cleanup\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4.4 Filter Metadata\n\n**Added in:** v1.31.0\n\n**Purpose:** Attach additional metadata to filter state for logging and observability.\n\n**Configuration:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  filter_metadata:\n    service_name: \"my-service\"\n    version: \"1.0\"\n    env: \"production\"\n```\n\n**Details:**\n- Structured as a protobuf Struct (key-value map)\n- Added to StreamInfo's filter state under the ext_proc filter namespace\n- Accessible in access logs and other filter state consumers\n- Helps with debugging and correlating logs across services\n\n**Implementation:**\n- Stored in FilterConfig as `filter_metadata_` member variable\n- Returned via `filterMetadata()` accessor method\n- Available to ExtProcLoggingInfo for export\n\n---\n\n## 5. Configuration Updates\n\n### 5.1 Complete Migration Checklist\n\nWhen upgrading from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0:\n\n- [ ] **If using `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:**\n  - Replace with `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n\n- [ ] **If using `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (or omitted):**\n  - Replace with `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (or omit; DEFAULT is implicit)\n\n- [ ] **If deploying observability use case:**\n  - Enable `observability_mode: true`\n  - Set `processing_mode` to use STREAMED body mode only\n  - Configure appropriate `deferred_close_timeout`\n\n- [ ] **If needing logging/debugging metadata:**\n  - Add `filter_metadata` with relevant key-value pairs\n\n- [ ] **Validate against Envoy:**\n  - Test configuration with `envoy --mode validate -c config.yaml`\n\n### 5.2 Side-by-Side Configuration Examples\n\n**v1.30.0 - Blocking External Processing with Cache Clearing Disabled**\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: BUFFERED\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        response_body_mode: BUFFERED\n      message_timeout: 2s\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 - Equivalent Configuration (Recommended)**\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      route_cache_action: RETAIN  # Replaces disable_clear_route_cache\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: BUFFERED\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        response_body_mode: BUFFERED\n      message_timeout: 2s\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 - New Observability Mode Configuration**\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: audit_service\n      failure_mode_allow: true  # Don't block on processor errors\n      observability_mode: true  # \"Send and Go\" mode\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: STREAMED  # Only STREAMED supported in observability mode\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        response_body_mode: STREAMED\n      deferred_close_timeout: 8s\n      filter_metadata:\n        environment: \"production\"\n        service_version: \"1.31.0\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Migration Steps\n\n### Step 1: Audit Current Configuration\n\nReview all ext_proc filter configurations:\n\n```bash\n# Find all ext_proc filter definitions\ngrep -r \"ext_proc\" envoy-config/\n```\n\nIdentify which configurations use:\n- `disable_clear_route_cache: true` \u2192 Need to migrate to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n- `disable_clear_route_cache: false` \u2192 Optional; can migrate to `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`\n\n### Step 2: Create v1.31.0 Compatible Configuration\n\nUpdate your configurations:\n\n```yaml\n# BEFORE (v1.30.0)\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# AFTER (v1.31.0)\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n### Step 3: Add Observability Features (Optional)\n\nIf implementing observability/monitoring use cases:\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5s\n  filter_metadata:\n    service: \"api-gateway\"\n    tier: \"edge\"\n```\n\n### Step 4: Validate Configuration\n\nTest with envoy configuration validator:\n\n```bash\nenvoy -c your-config.yaml --mode validate\n```\n\nExpected output on success:\n```\nconfiguration OK\n```\n\n### Step 5: Stage in Test Environment\n\n1. Deploy v1.31.0 Envoy with new configuration in staging\n2. Monitor for configuration errors in logs\n3. Verify external processor receives expected messages\n4. Check route cache behavior matches expectations\n\n### Step 6: Production Deployment\n\n1. Use canary deployment strategy\n2. Start with small traffic percentage (5-10%)\n3. Monitor processor latency and error rates\n4. Gradually increase traffic to 100%\n\n---\n\n## 7. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 7.1 Unit Test Scenarios\n\n**Test 1: route_cache_action DEFAULT Behavior**\n```\nSetup: route_cache_action: DEFAULT\nWhen: Processor returns clear_route_cache: true with header mutation\nThen: Route cache is cleared\n```\n\n**Test 2: route_cache_action CLEAR Behavior**\n```\nSetup: route_cache_action: CLEAR\nWhen: Processor returns header mutation\nThen: Route cache is cleared regardless of clear_route_cache flag\n```\n\n**Test 3: route_cache_action RETAIN Behavior**\n```\nSetup: route_cache_action: RETAIN\nWhen: Processor returns clear_route_cache: true\nThen: Route cache is NOT cleared; error counter incremented\n```\n\n**Test 4: Backward Compatibility**\n```\nSetup: disable_clear_route_cache: true\nWhen: Config is loaded\nThen: Internally converted to route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Test 5: Observability Mode**\n```\nSetup: observability_mode: true, processing_mode: STREAMED\nWhen: Request/response completes\nThen: Messages sent to processor without blocking; stream deferred-closed after timeout\n```\n\n### 7.2 Integration Test Scenarios\n\n1. **Deploy with observability_mode enabled:**\n   - Generate traffic through ext_proc filter\n   - Verify external processor receives all events\n   - Confirm main request path isn't blocked\n   - Check for processor response message errors (should be ignored)\n\n2. **Test route cache behavior:**\n   - Make requests that trigger header modifications\n   - Verify cache is cleared per route_cache_action setting\n   - Check metrics (clear_route_cache_ignored, clear_route_cache_disabled)\n\n3. **Test deferred close timeout:**\n   - Monitor gRPC stream lifetimes in observability mode\n   - Verify streams close within configured timeout\n   - Check for proper resource cleanup\n\n### 7.3 Validation Tests\n\nRun envoy config validator on your configurations:\n\n```bash\n# For each config file\nenvoy --config-path your-config.yaml --mode validate\n\n# Or validate all configs in a directory\nfind . -name \"*.yaml\" -exec envoy -c {} --mode validate \\;\n```\n\n---\n\n## 8. Rollback Guidance\n\n### 8.1 Quick Rollback Procedure\n\nIf issues occur after upgrading to v1.31.0:\n\n**Option 1: Revert to v1.30.0 Configuration Format**\n\nIf new features not critical, revert proto changes:\n\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 with new fields\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n  observability_mode: true\n\n# v1.30.0 compatible (removes new fields)\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: false\n  # Remove: observability_mode, deferred_close_timeout\n```\n\n**Option 2: Disable Problematic Features**\n\nKeep v1.31.0 but disable new features:\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Conservative default\n  observability_mode: false    # Disable Send and Go mode\n```\n\n**Option 3: Full Version Rollback**\n\nIf incompatibility detected:\n\n```bash\n# Rollback Envoy binary and configuration\ndocker pull envoyproxy/envoy:v1.30.0\n# Restart with old configuration\n```\n\n### 8.2 Common Issues and Solutions\n\n| Issue | Cause | Solution |\n|-------|-------|----------|\n| \"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time\" | Both old and new fields set | Use only `route_cache_action` field |\n| Processor not receiving responses in observability mode | Expected behavior | Remove responses from processor; they're ignored |\n| Streams staying open longer than expected | Deferred close timeout not reached | Reduce `deferred_close_timeout` value |\n| Route cache not cleared when expected | Wrong `route_cache_action` setting | Verify setting matches routing requirements |\n\n### 8.3 Health Checks During Rollback\n\nBefore declaring rollback complete:\n\n```bash\n# Check for error messages\nenvoy-logs | grep -i \"ext_proc.*error\"\n\n# Monitor processor connectivity\nenvoy-stats | grep ext_proc.streams_failed\n\n# Verify route cache behavior\nenvoy-stats | grep clear_route_cache\n\n# Check latency impact\nenvoy-metrics | grep request_time\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Behavioral Changes Summary\n\n### 9.1 Route Cache Behavior Changes\n\n| Scenario | v1.30.0 Behavior | v1.31.0 Behavior | Impact |\n|----------|-----------------|-----------------|--------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache=false`, processor sets `clear_route_cache=true` | Cache cleared | Cache cleared (DEFAULT) | None |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache=true`, processor sets `clear_route_cache=true` | Cache NOT cleared | Cache NOT cleared (RETAIN) | None |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache=false`, no header mutations | Cache not cleared | Cache not cleared | None |\n| New: `route_cache_action=CLEAR` | N/A | Cache ALWAYS cleared | **More aggressive caching**; use when processor modifies routing headers |\n\n### 9.2 Stream Management Changes\n\n| Aspect | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Impact |\n|--------|---------|---------|--------|\n| Stream closure on response complete | Immediate | Deferred (default 5s) | **More graceful shutdown**; allows cleanup |\n| In observability mode | N/A | Streams held open per timeout | **New feature** for non-blocking observability |\n| Resource cleanup | Not explicit | Explicit via ThreadLocalStreamManager | **Better resource management** |\n\n### 9.3 Configuration API Changes\n\n| Field | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Status |\n|-------|---------|---------|--------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | Required (boolean) | Deprecated | Use `route_cache_action` |\n| `route_cache_action` | N/A | New (enum) | Recommended |\n| `observability_mode` | N/A | New (boolean) | New feature |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | N/A | New (Duration) | New feature |\n| `filter_metadata` | N/A | New (Struct) | New feature |\n\n---\n\n## 10. Reference Documentation\n\n### 10.1 Proto Locations\n\n- **Configuration:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- **Processing Mode:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto`\n\n### 10.2 Implementation Files\n\n- **Filter Logic:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc` and `.h`\n- **Configuration:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/config.cc` and `.h`\n- **Processing State:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc` and `.h`\n- **Client Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.cc` and `.h`\n\n### 10.3 Key Code References\n\n| Feature | Location | Lines |\n|---------|----------|-------|\n| FilterConfig Constructor | ext_proc.cc | 179-224 |\n| Route Cache Action Logic | processor_state.cc | 440-461 |\n| ThreadLocalStreamManager | ext_proc.h | 148-199 |\n| Deferred Close Timeout | ext_proc.cc | 1383-1384 |\n| Observability Mode Sending | ext_proc.cc | 644+ |\n\n### 10.4 Documentation Links\n\n- **Configuration Reference:** `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`\n- **API Reference:** Envoy API docs for ExternalProcessor v3\n\n---\n\n## 11. FAQ\n\n**Q: Do I have to update `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action`?**\n\nA: Not immediately, but v1.31.0 supports both. Plan to migrate before the field is removed in a future version (likely v1.32+).\n\n**Q: Is observability_mode safe to enable in production?**\n\nA: With caution. Flow control is not yet implemented, so ensure your processor can handle the traffic rate. Monitor processor latency closely.\n\n**Q: What happens if my processor doesn't send responses in observability mode?**\n\nA: That's expected and correct. Envoy ignores responses in observability mode, so your processor can skip sending them.\n\n**Q: How does route_cache_action affect performance?**\n\nA: Clearing the route cache (DEFAULT or CLEAR) may trigger route re-evaluation, which has minimal overhead. RETAIN is most performant when routing changes are infrequent.\n\n**Q: Can I use observability_mode with BUFFERED body mode?**\n\nA: No. Only STREAMED body mode is supported. BUFFERED and BUFFERED_PARTIAL are automatically switched to STREAMED in observability mode.\n\n---\n\n## 12. {
  "content": "# Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) Filter Migration Guide\n## Version 1.30.0 to 1.31.0\n\n---\n\n## 1. Overview\n\nThis migration guide covers upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 (April 2024)** to **version 1.31.0 (July 2024)**.\n\nThe ext_proc filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses through a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy v1.31.0 introduces several enhancements focused on:\n\n- **Fine-grained route cache control** via a new `RouteCacheAction` enum\n- **Observability/monitoring mode** (\"Send and Go\") for non-blocking external processing\n- **Deferred stream closure** with configurable timeouts for clean resource management\n- **Better configuration semantics** with deprecation of boolean flags in favor of explicit enum values\n\n### Scope of Changes\n\nAll changes are in the **filter configuration API** and **internal stream management**. The external processor's gRPC service interface (ProcessingRequest/ProcessingResponse) remains unchanged.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Breaking Changes\n\n### 2.1 Route Cache Management Behavior Change\n\n**Change Type:** Configuration Option Deprecation + Behavior Refinement\n\n**Proto Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\nIn v1.30.0, route cache clearing was controlled by a single boolean field:\n\n```proto\n// v1.30.0\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n```\n\nIn v1.31.0, this has been superseded by an explicit enum with three options:\n\n```proto\n// v1.31.0\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Default: Obey the clear_route_cache flag from the external processor response\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear route cache (ignore clear_route_cache response flag)\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear route cache (ignore clear_route_cache response flag)\n  // Equivalent to old: disable_clear_route_cache = true\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n```\n\n**Impact:**\n- The old `disable_clear_route_cache` field is still accepted but **deprecated**\n- v1.31.0 automatically converts `disable_clear_route_cache=true` to `route_cache_action=RETAIN`\n- Using both fields with non-default values simultaneously is **not allowed** and will cause a validation error\n\n**Migration Example:**\n\n```yaml\n# v1.30.0 - Disable route cache clearing\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n\n# v1.31.0 - Equivalent configuration (recommended)\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Validation Details:**\n- If `disable_clear_route_cache=true` is specified, it's converted to `route_cache_action=RETAIN` (lines 213-221, ext_proc.cc)\n- If both fields have non-DEFAULT/non-true values, the config will be **rejected** with error:\n  ```\n  \"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time.\"\n  ```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Deprecated Features\n\n### 3.1 disable_clear_route_cache Field\n\n**Status:** Deprecated (but still functional for backward compatibility)\n\n**Timeline:** This field is marked for removal in a future Envoy version (likely v1.32+)\n\n**Migration Path:**\n\n| Old Config (`v1.30.0`) | New Config (`v1.31.0`) | Behavior |\n|---|---|---|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: false` | `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` | Follow clear_route_cache flag from processor |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache: true` | `route_cache_action: RETAIN` | Always ignore clear_route_cache flag |\n\n**Code References:**\n- v1.31.0 FilterConfig constructor: Lines 213-221 in `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc`\n- Proto field with migrate annotation: Lines 250-251 in `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\n**Deprecation Note:** The field is annotated with `field_migrate` annotation in the proto, indicating Envoy's intention to promote `route_cache_action` as the canonical field.\n\n---\n\n## 4. New Features\n\n### 4.1 RouteCacheAction Enum\n\n**Added in:** v1.31.0\n\n**Purpose:** Provide explicit, semantic control over route cache clearing behavior in response to processor modifications.\n\n**Usage:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR  # or DEFAULT, RETAIN\n```\n\n**Three Options:**\n\n1. **DEFAULT (0)** - Follow the processor response\n   - If processor sets `clear_route_cache=true` in response headers \u2192 clear cache\n   - Otherwise \u2192 keep cache as-is\n   - This is the default behavior if not specified\n\n2. **CLEAR (1)** - Always clear the route cache\n   - Route cache is cleared whenever the processor returns with header mutations\n   - Used when the processor frequently modifies headers that affect routing decisions\n   - Ensures routes are recomputed immediately\n\n3. **RETAIN (2)** - Never clear the route cache\n   - Route cache clearing requests from the processor are ignored\n   - Processor's `clear_route_cache` flag in CommonResponse is disregarded\n   - Useful when external processing doesn't affect routing\n\n**Implementation Details:**\n- Logic in `DecodingProcessorState::handleCommonHeaderResponse()` (processor_state.cc, lines 440-461)\n- The behavior only applies to downstream traffic (not upstream)\n- Route cache is only cleared when header mutations are present in the response\n\n---\n\n### 4.2 Observability Mode (\"Send and Go\")\n\n**Added in:** v1.31.0\n\n**Purpose:** Allow external processors to observe traffic without blocking the main request processing flow.\n\n**Configuration:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5000ms  # optional, default: 5000ms\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n\n| Aspect | Details |\n|--------|---------|\n| **Request Handling** | Messages sent to processor without waiting for responses |\n| **Response Blocking** | No blocking; filter continues processing immediately |\n| **Body Modes** | Only STREAMED mode is supported; BUFFERED/BUFFERED_PARTIAL ignored |\n| **Stream Closure** | Streams are deferred-closed after `deferred_close_timeout` |\n| **Use Case** | Logging, monitoring, security observability without latency impact |\n\n**Important Warnings:**\n- Flow control is **not yet implemented**\n- Fast senders (clients/servers) can overwhelm slow processors\n- Manual flow control implementation recommended in the processor service\n- See GitHub issue #33319 for flow control development status\n\n**Example Use Case:**\n```yaml\n# Monitor all traffic without affecting latency\next_proc:\n  grpc_service:\n    envoy_grpc:\n      cluster_name: security_observer\n  observability_mode: true\n  processing_mode:\n    request_header_mode: SEND\n    request_body_mode: STREAMED\n    response_header_mode: SEND\n    response_body_mode: STREAMED\n```\n\n**Implementation:**\n- Managed by `ThreadLocalStreamManager` and `DeferredDeletableStream` (ext_proc.h, lines 148-199)\n- Deferred closure uses Envoy dispatcher timers (ext_proc.cc, line 1384)\n- Observability mode logic in `Filter::sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` (ext_proc.cc, line 644+)\n\n---\n\n### 4.3 Deferred Close Timeout\n\n**Added in:** v1.31.0\n\n**Purpose:** Control how long gRPC streams to external processors remain open after the request/response completes.\n\n**Configuration:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  deferred_close_timeout: 5000ms  # 5 seconds (default)\n```\n\n**Details:**\n- **Default Value:** 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds)\n- **Valid Range:** 0 to 3600000 milliseconds (0 to 1 hour)\n- **Used In:** Observability mode and other scenarios requiring extended stream lifetime\n- **Purpose:** Prevent abrupt stream closure and allow graceful cleanup of resources\n\n**When It Matters:**\n- In observability mode, streams may outlive the HTTP request/response cycle\n- Allows processors to complete logging/monitoring work before disconnection\n- Prevents server-side processing errors from abrupt closure\n\n**Proto Field:**\n```proto\ngoogle.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n```\n\n**Example:**\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout: 10s  # Allow 10 seconds for deferred stream cleanup\n```\n\n---\n\n### 4.4 Filter Metadata\n\n**Added in:** v1.31.0\n\n**Purpose:** Attach additional metadata to filter state for logging and observability.\n\n**Configuration:**\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  grpc_service: ...\n  filter_metadata:\n    service_name: \"my-service\"\n    version: \"1.0\"\n    env: \"production\"\n```\n\n**Details:**\n- Structured as a protobuf Struct (key-value map)\n- Added to StreamInfo's filter state under the ext_proc filter namespace\n- Accessible in access logs and other filter state consumers\n- Helps with debugging and correlating logs across services\n\n**Implementation:**\n- Stored in FilterConfig as `filter_metadata_` member variable\n- Returned via `filterMetadata()` accessor method\n- Available to ExtProcLoggingInfo for export\n\n---\n\n## 5. Configuration Updates\n\n### 5.1 Complete Migration Checklist\n\nWhen upgrading from v1.30.0 to v1.31.0:\n\n- [ ] **If using `disable_clear_route_cache: true`:**\n  - Replace with `route_cache_action: RETAIN`\n\n- [ ] **If using `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (or omitted):**\n  - Replace with `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` (or omit; DEFAULT is implicit)\n\n- [ ] **If deploying observability use case:**\n  - Enable `observability_mode: true`\n  - Set `processing_mode` to use STREAMED body mode only\n  - Configure appropriate `deferred_close_timeout`\n\n- [ ] **If needing logging/debugging metadata:**\n  - Add `filter_metadata` with relevant key-value pairs\n\n- [ ] **Validate against Envoy:**\n  - Test configuration with `envoy --mode validate -c config.yaml`\n\n### 5.2 Side-by-Side Configuration Examples\n\n**v1.30.0 - Blocking External Processing with Cache Clearing Disabled**\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_service\n      failure_mode_allow: false\n      disable_clear_route_cache: true\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: BUFFERED\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        response_body_mode: BUFFERED\n      message_timeout: 2s\n```\n\n**v1.31.0 - New Observability Mode Configuration**\n\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: audit_service\n      failure_mode_allow: true  # Don't block on processor errors\n      observability_mode: true  # \"Send and Go\" mode\n      processing_mode:\n        request_header_mode: SEND\n        request_body_mode: STREAMED  # Only STREAMED supported in observability mode\n        response_header_mode: SEND\n        response_body_mode: STREAMED\n      deferred_close_timeout: 8s\n      filter_metadata:\n        environment: \"production\"\n        service_version: \"1.31.0\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Check route cache behavior matches expectations\n\n### Step 6: Production Deployment\n\n1. Use canary deployment strategy\n2. Start with small traffic percentage (5-10%)\n3. Monitor processor latency and error rates\n4. Gradually increase traffic to 100%\n\n---\n\n## 7. Testing Recommendations\n\n### 7.1 Unit Test Scenarios\n\n**Test 1: route_cache_action DEFAULT Behavior**\n```\nSetup: route_cache_action: DEFAULT\nWhen: Processor returns clear_route_cache: true with header mutation\nThen: Route cache is cleared\n```\n\n**Test 2: route_cache_action CLEAR Behavior**\n```\nSetup: route_cache_action: CLEAR\nWhen: Processor returns header mutation\nThen: Route cache is cleared regardless of clear_route_cache flag\n```\n\n**Test 3: route_cache_action RETAIN Behavior**\n```\nSetup: route_cache_action: RETAIN\nWhen: Processor returns clear_route_cache: true\nThen: Route cache is NOT cleared; error counter incremented\n```\n\n**Test 4: Backward Compatibility**\n```\nSetup: disable_clear_route_cache: true\nWhen: Config is loaded\nThen: Internally converted to route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\n**Test 5: Observability Mode**\n```\nSetup: observability_mode: true, processing_mode: STREAMED\nWhen: Request/response completes\nThen: Messages sent to processor without blocking; stream deferred-closed after timeout\n```\n\n### 7.2 Integration Test Scenarios\n\n1. **Deploy with observability_mode enabled:**\n   - Generate traffic through ext_proc filter\n   - Verify external processor receives all events\n   - Confirm main request path isn't blocked\n   - Check for processor response message errors (should be ignored)\n\n2. **Test route cache behavior:**\n   - Make requests that trigger header modifications\n   - Verify cache is cleared per route_cache_action setting\n   - Check metrics (clear_route_cache_ignored, clear_route_cache_disabled)\n\n3. **Test deferred close timeout:**\n   - Monitor gRPC stream lifetimes in observability mode\n   - Verify streams close within configured timeout\n   - Check for proper resource cleanup\n\n### 7.3 Validation Tests\n\nRun envoy config validator on your configurations:\n\n```bash\n# For each config file\nenvoy --config-path your-config.yaml --mode validate\n\n# Or validate all configs in a directory\nfind . -name \"*.yaml\" -exec envoy -c {} --mode validate \\;\n```\n\n---\n\n## 8. Rollback Guidance\n\n### 8.1 Quick Rollback Procedure\n\nIf issues occur after upgrading to v1.31.0:\n\n**Option 1: Revert to v1.30.0 Configuration Format**\n\nIf new features not critical, revert proto changes:\n\n```yaml\n# v1.31.0 with new fields\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: CLEAR\n  observability_mode: true\n\n# v1.30.0 compatible (removes new fields)\next_proc:\n  disable_clear_route_cache: false\n  # Remove: observability_mode, deferred_close_timeout\n```\n\n**Option 2: Disable Problematic Features**\n\nKeep v1.31.0 but disable new features:\n\n```yaml\next_proc:\n  route_cache_action: DEFAULT  # Conservative default\n  observability_mode: false    # Disable Send and Go mode\n```\n\n**Option 3: Full Version Rollback**\n\nIf incompatibility detected:\n\n```bash\n# Rollback Envoy binary and configuration\ndocker pull envoyproxy/envoy:v1.30.0\n# Restart with old configuration\n```\n\n### 8.2 Common Issues and Solutions\n\n| Issue | Cause | Solution |\n|-------|-------|----------|\n| \"disable_clear_route_cache and route_cache_action can not be set to none-default at the same time\" | Both old and new fields set | Use only `route_cache_action` field |\n| Processor not receiving responses in observability mode | Expected behavior | Remove responses from processor; they're ignored |\n| Streams staying open longer than expected | Deferred close timeout not reached | Reduce `deferred_close_timeout` value |\n| Route cache not cleared when expected | Wrong `route_cache_action` setting | Verify setting matches routing requirements |\n\n### 8.3 Health Checks During Rollback\n\nBefore declaring rollback complete:\n\n```bash\n# Check for error messages\nenvoy-logs | grep -i \"ext_proc.*error\"\n\n# Monitor processor connectivity\nenvoy-stats | grep ext_proc.streams_failed\n\n# Verify route cache behavior\nenvoy-stats | grep clear_route_cache\n\n# Check latency impact\nenvoy-metrics | grep request_time\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Behavioral Changes Summary\n\n### 9.1 Route Cache Behavior Changes\n\n| Scenario | v1.30.0 Behavior | v1.31.0 Behavior | Impact |\n|----------|-----------------|-----------------|--------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache=false`, processor sets `clear_route_cache=true` | Cache cleared | Cache cleared (DEFAULT) | None |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache=true`, processor sets `clear_route_cache=true` | Cache NOT cleared | Cache NOT cleared (RETAIN) | None |\n| `disable_clear_route_cache=false`, no header mutations | Cache not cleared | Cache not cleared | None |\n| New: `route_cache_action=CLEAR` | N/A | Cache ALWAYS cleared | **More aggressive caching**; use when processor modifies routing headers |\n\n### 9.2 Stream Management Changes\n\n| Aspect | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Impact |\n|--------|---------|---------|--------|\n| Stream closure on response complete | Immediate | Deferred (default 5s) | **More graceful shutdown**; allows cleanup |\n| In observability mode | N/A | Streams held open per timeout | **New feature** for non-blocking observability |\n| Resource cleanup | Not explicit | Explicit via ThreadLocalStreamManager | **Better resource management** |\n\n### 9.3 Configuration API Changes\n\n| Field | v1.30.0 | v1.31.0 | Status |\n|-------|---------|---------|--------|\n| `disable_clear_route_cache` | Required (boolean) | Deprecated | Use `route_cache_action` |\n| `route_cache_action` | N/A | New (enum) | Recommended |\n| `observability_mode` | N/A | New (boolean) | New feature |\n| `deferred_close_timeout` | N/A | New (Duration) | New feature |\n| `filter_metadata` | N/A | New (Struct) | New feature |\n\n---\n\n## 10. Reference Documentation\n\n### 10.1 Proto Locations\n\n- **Configuration:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- **Processing Mode:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto`\n\n### 10.2 Implementation Files\n\n- **Filter Logic:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.cc` and `.h`\n- **Configuration:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/config.cc` and `.h`\n- **Processing State:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/processor_state.cc` and `.h`\n- **Client Implementation:** `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/client_impl.cc` and `.h`\n\n### 10.3 Key Code References\n\n| Feature | Location | Lines |\n|---------|----------|-------|\n| FilterConfig Constructor | ext_proc.cc | 179-224 |\n| Route Cache Action Logic | processor_state.cc | 440-461 |\n| ThreadLocalStreamManager | ext_proc.h | 148-199 |\n| Deferred Close Timeout | ext_proc.cc | 1383-1384 |\n| Observability Mode Sending | ext_proc.cc | 644+ |\n\n### 10.4 Documentation Links\n\n- **Configuration Reference:** `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`\n- **API Reference:** Envoy API docs for ExternalProcessor v3\n\n---\n\n## 11. FAQ\n\n**Q: Do I have to update `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action`?**\n\nA: Not immediately, but v1.31.0 supports both. Plan to migrate before the field is removed in a future version (likely v1.32+).\n\n**Q: Is observability_mode safe to enable in production?**\n\nA: With caution. Flow control is not yet implemented, so ensure your processor can handle the traffic rate. Monitor processor latency closely.\n\n**Q: What happens if my processor doesn't send responses in observability mode?**\n\nA: That's expected and correct. Envoy ignores responses in observability mode, so your processor can skip sending them.\n\n**Q: How does route_cache_action affect performance?**\n\nA: Clearing the route cache (DEFAULT or CLEAR) may trigger route re-evaluation, which has minimal overhead. RETAIN is most performant when routing changes are infrequent.\n\n**Q: Can I use observability_mode with BUFFERED body mode?**\n\nA: No. Only STREAMED body mode is supported. BUFFERED and BUFFERED_PARTIAL are automatically switched to STREAMED in observability mode.\n\n---\n\n## 12. 1. WRITE /workspace/documentation.md
# Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) Filter Migration Guide
## Version 1.30.0 to 1.31.0

---

## 1. Overview

This migration guide covers upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 (April 2024)** to **version 1.31.0 (July 2024)**.

The ext_proc filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses through a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy v1.31.0 introduces several enhancements focused on:

- **Fine-grained route cache control** via a new `RouteCacheAction` enum
- **Observability/monitoring mode** ("Send and Go") for non-blocking external processing
- **Deferred stream closure** with configurable timeouts for clean resource management
- **Better configuration semantics** with deprecation of boolean flags in favor of explicit enum values

### Scope of Changes

All changes are in the **filter configuration API** and **internal stream management**. The external processor's gRPC service interface (ProcessingRequest/ProcessingResponse) remains unchanged.

---

## 2. Breaking Changes

### 2.1 Route Cache Management Behavior Change

**Change Type:** Configuration Option Deprecation + Behavior Refinement

**Proto Location:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`

In v1.30.0, route cache clearing was controlled by a single boolean field:

```proto
// v1.30.0
bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;
```

In v1.31.0, this has been superseded by an explicit enum with three options:

```proto
// v1.31.0
enum RouteCacheAction {
  // Default: Obey the clear_route_cache flag from the external processor response
  DEFAULT = 0;

  // Always clear route cache (ignore clear_route_cache response flag)
  CLEAR = 1;

  // Never clear route cache (ignore clear_route_cache response flag)
  // Equivalent to old: d
... (truncated)
